  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_028de478-53f0-4f19-86e4-cf5ec078c641'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer6894842862128902133"><i>Mighty Kushiel, of rod and weal<br/>Late of the brazen portals<br/>With blood-tipp'd dart a wound unhealed<br/>Pricks the eyen of chosen mortals</i><br/><br/>The land of Terre d'Ange is a place of unsurpassed beauty and grace. H</span>
  <span id="freeText6894842862128902133" style="display:none"><i>Mighty Kushiel, of rod and weal<br />Late of the brazen portals<br />With blood-tipp'd dart a wound unhealed<br />Pricks the eyen of chosen mortals</i><br /><br />The land of Terre d'Ange is a place of unsurpassed beauty and grace. The inhabiting race rose from the seed of angels and men, and they live by one simple rule: <i>Love as thou wilt.</i><br /><br />Phèdre nó Delaunay was sold into indentured servitude as a child. Her bond was purchased by a nobleman, the first to recognize that she is one pricked by Kushiel's Dart, chosen to forever experience pain and pleasure as one. He trained Phèdre in the courtly arts and the talents of the bedchamber—and, above all, the ability to observe, remember, and analyze.<br /><br />When she stumbled upon a plot that threatened the very foundations of her homeland, she gave up almost everything she held dear to save it. She survived, and lived to have others tell her story, and if they embellished the tale with fabric of mythical splendor, they weren't far off the mark.<br /><br />The hands of the gods weigh heavily upon Phèdre's brow, and they are not finished with her. While the young queen who sits upon the throne is well loved by the people, there are those who believe another should wear the crown... and those who escaped the wrath of the mighty are not yet done with their schemes for power and revenge.<br /><br />Cover art by John Jude Palencar</span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/464719-so-i-ve-read-kushiel-s-dart-and-wonder-if">So, I&#39;ve read Kushiel&#39;s Dart and wonder if it&#39;s worth it to read Kushiel&#39;s Chosen? A lot of people seem to love it but I&#39;ve read some reviews that say Phedre&#39;s character gets quite annoying. Others seem to think it&#39;s kind of a rehash of the first book but not as epic. And finally, Joscelin&#39;s character doesn&#39;t seem to be in this book that much which I think is a huge miss.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/32328420-john-mendez"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_100x100-c7bfe730633c9983e27caaa66a8e244a.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/32328420-john-mendez">John Mendez</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I just finished listening to this audiobook yesterday. First of all Joscelin is in it plenty, it's Hyacynth who's missing. <br/><br/>I thought the first book wa<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I just finished listening to this audiobook yesterday. First of all Joscelin is in it plenty, it's Hyacynth who's missing. <br /><br />I thought the first book was quite a bit more charming, the characters forgot their lessons from the first book. The prose was just as good as book one, maybe better in places if you can overlook the fact that there is so much less lore in this book than the first (I like reading worldbuilding/lore quite a bit). Plot wise, it was almost as if the author re-used a small parts of the first book's plot. I liked book 1 better due to the lore and how Phedre's perspective changed from pawn to player, whereas in this book I didn't get a sense that Phedre became a substantially better player.<br /><br />So... maybe?<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1685767470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1685767470" />
    <a title="mark monday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday"><img alt="mark monday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572672245p2/131922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1685767470?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mark monday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mark monday" href="/user/show/131922-mark-monday">mark monday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=fantasy-modern">fantasy-modern</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1685767470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6781709664464272288">I was waffling between 3 & 4 stars on this one, but since the second book in this series was a marked improvement for me on the first book, 4 stars it is.<br/><br/>our intrepid heroine Phèdre - courtesan supreme with a very special talent for transmuting pain into pleasure - makes her debut redux as a titled Lady and so re-enters various schemes and plots at a very different level. and with that elimination of class issues (as well as the death of her charming <s>pimp</s> patron in the first book) came the erasu</span>
  <span id="freeText6781709664464272288" style="display:none">I was waffling between 3 &amp; 4 stars on this one, but since the second book in this series was a marked improvement for me on the first book, 4 stars it is.<br /><br />our intrepid heroine Phèdre - courtesan supreme with a very special talent for transmuting pain into pleasure - makes her debut redux as a titled Lady and so re-enters various schemes and plots at a very different level. and with that elimination of class issues (as well as the death of her charming <s>pimp</s> patron in the first book) came the erasure of a lot of what annoyed me previously. which is odd because I love reading books about class warfare. maybe I am just a softie though, because I'd prefer to read about such things from the perspective of a fully empowered and independent woman capable of making her own decisions rather than reading about it from the perspective of a woman used as a pawn and sex puppet-cum-spy. the word "cum" in that last sentence was used in the formal, non-pornographic sense so keep your minds out of the gutter, pervs. and it's not like there's much class warfare in either book anyway - the appeal of these books rest in the heavy-breathing erotic atmosphere combined with all sorts of courtly intrigue.<br /><br />which is kept front and center. what a relief! no gallivanting off to versions of Germania and Brittania to have eye-rolling adventures involving barbarians and swordplay and torture. Carey does a fabulous job in making these intrigues as compelling as any battle. her versions of France and Italy are wonderful creations and I was salivating over the combination of ambiguous character motivations, political machinations full of sneaky feints and double-edged words, assassination plots, and a search for a thoroughly enchanting villainess, all delivered amidst delightfully lush descriptions of the various locales through which Phèdre and her retinue travel. it was all quite delicious - a tasty meal.<br /><br />other observations:<br /><br />magic was kept at a minimum. it was handled poorly in the first book; its appearance here (during a sojourn in a version of Crete) was a bit painful but thankfully brief.<br /><br />love story was front and center. still rather annoying but this time I did sort of feel for poor Joscelin. must be hard to have a girlfriend who still rents herself out, despite being a Lady of the Court.<br /><br />the mythology of this world, featuring Elua (Jesus' sorta son) and his fallen angel companions, was as absorbing as ever.<br /><br />it was nice to see a sadistic top actually portrayed as a good guy. well, not a bad guy, at least. the first book's bdsm trappings ended up feeling a bit hypocritical when all of its s&amp;m tops were clearly villainous assholes. that's not the case here. Severio (ha! that name!) may be a spoiled, grouchy fratboy of a prince, but he's not evil and is actually pretty supportive once he realizes his tastes don't automatically make him a monster. he just needed to find a partner like Lady Phèdre to make him feel okay with himself. aww! and all that said, I was thankful that the bdsm scenes that dominated the first novel were minimized in this book. I guess I'm just not a big fan of that sort of stuff (anymore).<br /><br />I also finally began to understand why, sexually, our heroine is <i>a very special person</i>. in the first book, I found the assertion that no one like her had been born in hundreds of years to be a bit hard to swallow - getting some degree of pleasure from some forms of pain is not exactly a super-rare attribute. thousands of fetish sites can surely attest to that. however this book provided a couple eye-opening examples: Phèdre going into orgasmic convulsions when being angrily shaken by Joscelin and, more amusingly, after getting pricked by a seamstress' needle while being fitted for one of her typically gorgeous gowns. okay Phèdre, I get it, you are definitely a very special person. don't let anyone tell you otherwise!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6781709664464272288" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2264156339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2264156339" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2264156339?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=alternative-history">alternative-history</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2264156339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17781332837588321215"><b>*** 4.35 ***<br/><br/>A Buddy Read with the FBR group! </b><br/><br/>This second book in the Phedre Trilogy was, in my opinion, better than the first. The pacing was much better and it kept you on your toes throughout. It had some lull moments, but they were well spaced and gave the main heroine time for some angst and going through all the facts and things she had done wrong and has to plan to do still... The more dynamic format might have positively been assisted by the smaller page count, although at 678 pages it is</span>
  <span id="freeText17781332837588321215" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.35 ***<br /><br />A Buddy Read with the FBR group! </b><br /><br />This second book in the Phedre Trilogy was, in my opinion, better than the first. The pacing was much better and it kept you on your toes throughout. It had some lull moments, but they were well spaced and gave the main heroine time for some angst and going through all the facts and things she had done wrong and has to plan to do still... The more dynamic format might have positively been assisted by the smaller page count, although at 678 pages it is still a hefty tome. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“Why is there ever this perverse cruelty in humankind, that makes us hurt most those we love best?” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />This book starts about an year after the end of the first. You would have thought that Countess Phèdre nó Delaunay would be satisfied with her new title, estates, and the love of the man she seems to love as well, the ex-warrior monk Joscelin, but the Chosen of Kushiel doesn't seem to be satisfied with kicking her heels in the genteel country society, so she decides to take the bate and go on a search for the treacherous and very alluring vileness Melisande Shahirizai , who escaped her imprisonment and death sentence. In order to pursue her quarry she goes back to the seat of the royal family and rededicates herself to the goddess Namaah, thinking that by bedding as many nobles as she could, she might find who conspired and helped Melisande, and might be able to figure out where to find and detain her. This of course puts a big dent into the relationship she has with Joscelin and that comes to a complete halt when he decides to start studding with this alternative World's Christians, who actually read much more like the Hasidim Jews of our world. He fits perfectly with them, since they have been promised in a prophecy a country of their own, and he gets to train them to fight. Things between him and Phedre really go bad and this rift comes in play when he is not there to protect her. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“And having once chosen, never to seek to return to the crossroads of that decision-for even if one chooses wrongly, the choice cannot be unmade.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Meanwhile, Phedre gets introduced to a young noble with a temper, a brother and sister who love to chat about court intrigue, a very crabby prince and another beautiful and charismatic woman, which Jacqueline Carey is obviously very good at writing. Queen Ysandre de la Courcey puts on a good show as well, but nothing and no one can compare with Melisande Shahirizai and the heat that comes off the pages when she is in any proximity to Phedre!!! Wow! I hate her, because she is infinitely cruel, but I can't help but love her too!!! Now that is a women of which even the big boys have to be terrified! Good for girl power, but still a bad person in the end....<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“They are fools, who reckon Elua a soft god, fit only for the worship of starry-eyed lovers. Let the warriors clamor after gods of blood and thunder; love is hard, harder than steel and thrice as cruel. It is as inexorable as the tides, and life and death alike follow in it's wake.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />I love the mish-mash of cultures, religions, deities, and characters so much, that I even choose to overlook the heavy irregularities of time periods of different countries co-existing at the same time in the Ms. Carey's world. I will go with "this is Fantasy" so things like that can happen and it is OK! I also love that in the main land where Phedre comes from, love is acceptable in all forms as long as it is between consenting adults. Yes, this whole series is full of sexual relationships - after all, Phedre is a servant of Namaah, which makes her a highly paid prostitute and is also chosen by Kushiel. which makes her really appreciative of the pain and domination which comes with it at times. So yeah, she is using her skills as a sex professional to spy for Queen and Country!!! She is a true patriot:):):):) <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“The pain of the flesh is naught to that of the heart” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />If you are willing to accept the sex as just her job and take it as a background, this story is actually pure adventure and very good one at that! I was even toying with going for 5 stars, but there were things I couldn't overlook, so almost 5 stars it is. I am very glad that some friends encouraged me to start the series and I am looking forward to the next installment with trepidation!!! You have to give it a try! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“If you thought better of me, you would not be so surprised” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and many more wonderful Books to come! </span>
  <a data-text-id="17781332837588321215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_27396295" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27396295" />
    <a title="Nicky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/223837-nicky"><img alt="Nicky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308224598p2/223837.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27396295?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=historical-fiction-alternatehistory">historical-fiction-alternatehistory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=queer">queer</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27396295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9701919882757542902">With the expectations Kushiel's Dart gave me, I might have been worried that Kushiel's Chosen wouldn't match up. I wasn't, but I wouldn't have needed to be anyway. I loved this book just as much as the first one. Everything I've said about how it's not for everyone still stands (see my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27396293' rel='nofollow noopener'>first review</a>), although there was less sex, I think, and perhaps more of the politics. Somehow, this book didn't feel as dense as that one, but there's still a lot of content considering it's the second book of a </span>
  <span id="freeText9701919882757542902" style="display:none">With the expectations Kushiel's Dart gave me, I might have been worried that Kushiel's Chosen wouldn't match up. I wasn't, but I wouldn't have needed to be anyway. I loved this book just as much as the first one. Everything I've said about how it's not for everyone still stands (see my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27396293" rel="nofollow noopener">first review</a>), although there was less sex, I think, and perhaps more of the politics. Somehow, this book didn't feel as dense as that one, but there's still a lot of content considering it's the second book of a trilogy, and not a trilogy in itself. I think the feeling of less going on is mostly because there are fewer dramatic changes -- in the first book, there were a lot of milestones, and in this one, maybe not as much. It's still an incredible ride.<br /><br />The stage is set, in this book, so there isn't such a flurry of characters being thrown at you. The new ones, such as Nicola L'Envers y Aragon and Sevario Stregazza, are quite interesting (not least because of the sex scenes, I have to admit). It's lovely to see how Jacqueline Carey weaves the characters so neatly into the plot -- there are no useless characters. I was sorry not to see anything of Hyacinthe in this book, and I was glad that he wasn't <i>ignored</i>. Ysandre was one of my favourite characters in the latter part of this book: she's written as such a strong, strong character.<br /><br />The relationship between Joscelin and Phèdre was more painful than ever in this book, so I was very, very glad of the end. I'm not sure it could have continued as it was without getting needlessly painful and boring. While the new development makes me happy now, I have no doubts that Joscelin and Phèdre will find new ways to hurt my heart -- and that's good. The relationship between Melisande and Phèdre is still wonderfully handled. The thin line between love and hate that lies between them is perfectly walked. The scene where Phèdre smashes her head back against something to distract herself from Melisande's kiss is <i>amazing</i>.<br /><br />Plotwise, it was <i>so good</i>. It seriously surprised me in various places, leaving me to flail and keyboard bash and fangirl at anyone willing to listen. The twists and turns are surprising, and yet brilliantly set up: once it's happened you think, "Oh. Yes. Of course."<br /><br />There's a lovely conclusion, ending the book with some closure and yet also with threads still waiting to be tied up in the final book of the trilogy. I can't wait. I'm tempted to buy the Imriel books already, but I think I'll wait until they're all out in paperback -- painful as that will be.<br /><br />I seriously recommend this trilogy, if you don't mind a bit of BDSM sex woven into the plot (you can skip it, after all).</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12354355178856971946">Perhaps some day I will read one of these BDSM courtesan-spy epic fantasy doorstops and actually be able to talk about it afterwards, but today is not that day. Because right now, I am just so fucking grateful to this book, it has eclipsed the book itself – unintentionally hilarious, strangely unproblematic – almost entirely. This is what I read during the final two weeks of my last semester in law school. It’s what I read on the eight minute dog walking breaks, what I read when I snapped awake </span>
  <span id="freeText12354355178856971946" style="display:none">Perhaps some day I will read one of these BDSM courtesan-spy epic fantasy doorstops and actually be able to talk about it afterwards, but today is not that day. Because right now, I am just so fucking grateful to this book, it has eclipsed the book itself – unintentionally hilarious, strangely unproblematic – almost entirely. This is what I read during the final two weeks of my last semester in law school. It’s what I read on the eight minute dog walking breaks, what I read when I snapped awake at 4:30 in the morning but just could not face studying more right then, what I read when I took a half-hour breather twelve-hours out from the end when the euphoria started setting in, it’s what I read on the train in to my exams. And you know, there were pirates! And prison breaks! And kinky lesbian sex scenes! And great battles! But I barely noticed, because this book was pleasant in a white noise kind of way, and it was long so I didn’t have to face finding something else to read, and it just tra-la-la’ed along for 600 pages whether I was paying attention or not. Basically it was the book equivalent of someone quietly holding your hand and telling you about their day just so you could listen to the sound of their voice and not worry about the sense of it.<br /><br />Oh my God, Jacqueline Carey. Thank you thank you thank you.<br /></span>

<div id="review_151254410" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Bob/Sally" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally"><img alt="Bob/Sally" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598307870p2/2224905.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151254410?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bob/Sally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bob/Sally" href="/user/show/2224905-bob-sally">Bob/Sally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=female-author">female-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=female-fronted-fantasy">female-fronted-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2224905-bob-sally?shelf=fantasy-epic">fantasy-epic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151254410" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16998660702065687200">It's funny what the years can do to your taste in books - and I'm talking about something deeper, something more profound than those books that just don't stand up to being revisited. Instead, I'm talking about those books that you appreciated back in the day, but somehow knew you weren't quite ready to enjoy. Books that linger somewhere in the back of your imagination, biding their time until you're ready to continue with the series.<br/><br/>Kushiel's Chosen, the second book of the Kushiel's Legacy seri</span>
  <span id="freeText16998660702065687200" style="display:none">It's funny what the years can do to your taste in books - and I'm talking about something deeper, something more profound than those books that just don't stand up to being revisited. Instead, I'm talking about those books that you appreciated back in the day, but somehow knew you weren't quite ready to enjoy. Books that linger somewhere in the back of your imagination, biding their time until you're ready to continue with the series.<br /><br />Kushiel's Chosen, the second book of the Kushiel's Legacy series by Jacqueline Carey, was the first book to really open my eyes to this. I would have been in my 20's when I read Kushiel's Dart, just out of University, and stumbling my way into a career. I remember there being a definite taboo appeal to the story, with the book itself representing something of a game-changer for me at the time. It was a graduation of sorts from the pages of traditional fantasy to something . . . well, more.<br /><br />It was late last year that I finally got around to reading the second book in the series (prompted by a review copy of the new trade paperback edition), and I was finally ready to appreciate it. This is a series that offers up a blend of fetish and fantasy, spiritualism and sadomasochism, hedonism and heroism. More than that, it is an epic fantasy with the most profound of messages at its heart - "Love as thou wilt.” As powerful and original as I remember the first book being, the second revealed itself to be an even stronger read. In moving beyond that taboo novelty of its sexuality, I was able to appreciate the characters, the politics, the mythology, and the storytelling.<br /><br />Yes, it's a romantic fantasy, but the political intrigues are as strong as anything you'll find in more traditional fantasies. It's a big, sweeping series, often heavy on both the head and the heart, and one that I found I'd finally grown into. The taboo element is still there, and still permeates the series, but it's become an accent rather than the story's defining element.<br /><br /><br /><i>Originally reviewed at <a href="http://beauty-in-ruins.blogspot.ca/2016/08/growing-into-fantasy-with-carey-haydon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty in Ruins</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16998660702065687200" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_154894792" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154894792" />
    <a title="Sarah Mac" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac"><img alt="Sarah Mac" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499925811p2/4490376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154894792?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Mac" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Mac" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac">Sarah Mac</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=cover-me-brown">cover-me-brown</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=fantasy-soap-and-romance">fantasy-soap-and-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2015-leftovers-completed">zzz-2015-leftovers-completed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2015">zzz-2015</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=hoopy-good-reads">hoopy-good-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=epic-doorstoppers">epic-doorstoppers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154894792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12161512497925040530">Another beautifully written epic fantasy.<br/><br/><i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> picks up where <i>Kushiel's Dart</i> left off. But whereas Phedre is initially drawn into intrigue for the sake of her murdered mentor & foster-brother, the tragedies & travails in this second installment are a product of Phedre's own impetus. She doesn't have to become involved, but she makes that choice -- the same way she submits to a patron's whims, but on a larger political scale. Likewise, the intrigue in this book has a more personal note</span>
  <span id="freeText12161512497925040530" style="display:none">Another beautifully written epic fantasy.<br /><br /><i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> picks up where <i>Kushiel's Dart</i> left off. But whereas Phedre is initially drawn into intrigue for the sake of her murdered mentor &amp; foster-brother, the tragedies &amp; travails in this second installment are a product of Phedre's own impetus. She doesn't have to become involved, but she makes that choice -- the same way she submits to a patron's whims, but on a larger political scale. Likewise, the intrigue in this book has a more personal note. Vanquished is the onslaught of brutal Viking-esque hordes; this time the peril is pretty faces &amp; nobility in the heart of Terre d'Ange, &amp; that duplicity spurs her decision to resume the chess game with Melisande.<br /><br />Phedre is that rare breed in fantasy -- a strong female character who isn't a warrior, or even royalty. Rather, she's a highly-placed courtesan whose principle talents are looking beautiful on cue, submissive sex, unraveling of political tangles, dicing with soldiers, &amp; a tenacious survival instinct. She has a definite prejudice toward the perfection of all things D'Angeline, yet she is quick to appreciate simple goodness &amp; beauty in other cultures. And though she admits a preference for creature comforts, she values loyalty &amp; kindred souls above all else. <br /><br />I can't help thinking this author must have devoured bodice rippers when she was younger. Phedre's sprawling adventures -- bouncing from place to place &amp; one impossible situation to the next, all the while repeatedly separated from Joscelin &amp; her closest companions -- smack of classic bodice shredding. But her unabashed femininity &amp; sexual responses are also reminiscent of free-wheeling doorstoppers with kaleidoscopic covers. So many heroines these days are ashamed of having sexual thoughts, let alone sleeping with men who aren't the primary hero. Where's the fun in that? Why is larger-than-life such a dirty concept these days?! The written world needs more Phedres, dammit. <br /><br />...But I still hate that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Remy &amp; Fortun <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> were killed. ;____; Curse you, Jacqueline Carey.<br /><br />Not as intense as #1, but still worth the high rating; the characters make up for any slow parts of the story, &amp; the precisely elegant narration is a balm to my brain.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12161512497925040530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_40009844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40009844" />
    <a title="Kara Babcock" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1188122-kara-babcock"><img alt="Kara Babcock" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580776593p2/1188122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40009844?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kara Babcock" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kara Babcock" href="/user/show/1188122-kara-babcock">Kara Babcock</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=2010-read">2010-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1188122-kara-babcock?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40009844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15200546598922442035">Screw magic. Give me some political fantasy any day, and I'm a happy reader.<br/><br/>I <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40009839' rel='nofollow noopener'>liked <i>Kushiel's Dart</i></a>. I'm not sure if there's a definite quality improvement or if I'm going too easy on this one, but I loved <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i>.<br/><br/>The Kushiel's Legacy series takes place in a sort of <a href='http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/FantasyCounterpartCulture' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Counterpart Culture</a> world where it's Europe, only not. From this starting point, Jacqueline Carey creates a world that, while somewhat similar to our own, nevertheless has unique societies and politics. As she crisscr</span>
  <span id="freeText15200546598922442035" style="display:none">Screw magic. Give me some political fantasy any day, and I'm a happy reader.<br /><br />I <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40009839" rel="nofollow noopener">liked <i>Kushiel's Dart</i></a>. I'm not sure if there's a definite quality improvement or if I'm going too easy on this one, but I loved <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i>.<br /><br />The Kushiel's Legacy series takes place in a sort of <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/FantasyCounterpartCulture" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Counterpart Culture</a> world where it's Europe, only not. From this starting point, Jacqueline Carey creates a world that, while somewhat similar to our own, nevertheless has unique societies and politics. As she crisscrosses Europe—sorry, <i>Europa</i>—in search of the escaped traitor, Melisande Shahirizai, Phèdre tours many of these societies and inevitably gets involved in her politics. The combination of her stunning beauty, sexual promiscuity, and savvy spy skills can be very persuasive.<br /><br />Indeed, it's quite possible to label Phèdre a <a href="http://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Main/MarySue" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary Sue</a> and call it day. That doesn't do justice to Carey's intricate plotting though. Rather, I love <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> because it teeters on the brink of being contrived; Phèdre balances just on the precipice of Mary Sue-dom. All these people Phèdre encounter tend to help her, for one or more of the three aforementioned character traits she possesses. To put it in perspective: upon escaping from an inescapable island prison (and nearly drowning), Phèdre soon rebuilds her power base, befriending in the process not one but <i>two</i> other nations, and returns to Venice—sorry, La Serenissima—to stop the assassination of her Queen.<br /><br />What saves the book, and Phèdre, is the difficulty level at which Carey has set her game. Despite her ever-ready allies, despite her shrewdness and knowledge of political intrigue, Phèdre spends most of the book suffering failure after failure. It's like Carey has constructed a giant locked room mystery (where the room is the size of a continent), and Phèdre has interrogated all of the witnesses and suspects, but she <i>still</i> guesses wrongly. Meanwhile, I guessed where Melisande was hiding long before the big reveal (and I <i>never</i> solve those mysteries). But does this make the book bad? On the contrary, it's very smart. By choosing it to do this way, Carey divides the book into two parts that are almost self-contained narratives in themselves, with introduction, rising action, climax, and denouement.<br /><br />In the first half of <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i>, we're re-introduced to Phèdre, Terre d'Ange, and being a Servant of Namaah. The main focus is on discovering how Melisande escaped custody at the end of <i>Kushiel's Dart</i> (and hence, where she has gone to ground). To this end, we're immersed in the court life in the City of Elua, with Phèdre unsure of who is trustworthy, since someone supposedly beyond reproach had to help Melisande escape. After staging a falling out with Queen Ysandre and relocating to La Serenissima, Phèdre soon discovers where Melisande is hiding. But it's too late, and she's imprisoned in an inescapable fortress on an island.<br /><br />The second half features Phèdre's lucky escape, several brushes with death, and the befriending and bedding of a pirate. The mystery is over, and now it's all about rebuilding her power base so Phèdre can return to La Serenissima in time to prevent Ysandre's assassination. It's pretty obvious that Phèdre will succeed at this one task, even if she has failed at everything else, so the source of the drama comes from everyone around Phèdre. Who lives and who dies? What's Melisande's fate? More importantly, how do the machinations of a D'Angeline traitor affect Serenissiman politics? Carey constantly impresses me with her ability to effortless manage <i>so many</i> characters. The universe of Kushiel's Legacy is very heavily populated, but not so much so that it's Name Soup.<br /><br /><i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> is sort of a political/spy thriller set in a fantasy world, albeit only in the sense that slow-moving historical fiction can be a thriller (as the events take place over the course of a year). It's weakest in its characterization, especially with Phèdre and Joscelin's relationship, which is far too prolonged. (Also, of all the exposition that Carey skips in the second book, she doesn't re-explain the nature of the Cassilines, something I had forgotten in the year that managed to elapse between books.)<br /><br />By far, the most intriguing relationship is the one between Phèdre and Melisande. They are each other's nemesis on both an intellectual and visceral level. Phèdre and I both admire Melisande's aptitude at the game of thrones. She is a delightfully crafty enemy and well a match for Phèdre—in more ways than one, as Phèdre considers Melisande <i>delicious</i> as well as delightful. If her existence as the world's only <i>anguissette</i> isn't conflicting enough, her attraction to Melisande is inconvenient and almost deadly. At first, I didn't entirely understand this aspect of their relationship—it's obvious, after all, that Phèdre would never betray Ysandre and join the dark side.<br /><br />But it's more than just mere attraction. Phèdre is a lonely heroine, and has been from the start of the series. After the deaths of Alcuin and Anafiel and the loss of Hyacinthe in <i>Kushiel's Dart</i>, Phèdre is more alone than ever. This situation only escalates throughout <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> as Phèdre alienates Joscelin and loses some of her companions. Moreover, wherever she goes and whatever she accomplishes, she is always still "the <i>anguissette</i>," identified sometimes more by myth than her own personality. (The fact that she saves the kingdom and is commended by Ysandre for this at the end of the book doesn't exactly help.)<br /><br />As her nemesis, Melisande is a part of Phèdre's identity. She beat Phèdre in the first halves of both books. Although Phèdre was ultimately victorious (twice), Melisande promises that it's not game over. Similarly, Melisande is the only patron of Phèdre's who ever extracted the safe word—sorry, <i>signale</i>—during a sexual exploit. I would go so far as to say that Melisande is the single person who best understands Phèdre, both as an <i>anguissette</i> and as spy—she certainly understands Phèdre better than Phèdre's love, Joscelin. At the best of times he's clueless about the complications of Phèdre's commitments to Namaah's service; at the worst of times he's openly disdainful.<br /><br />And so, <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> takes the best aspects of <i>Kushiel's Dart</i> and amplifies them, grafting on a better plot with more sinister intrigue and a stellar cast of supporting characters. More than just court drama (although Phèdre never hesitates to give us a play-by-play of what she's wearing), <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> is the intimate dance between two like minds conducted with an entire continent as their battlefield. Phèdre and Melisande face off in a conflict that is both deeply political and deeply personal. In so doing, Carey captures the breadth of human expression writ large and writ small.<br /><br />Returning to Terre D'Ange and Phèdre's Europe—sorry, <i>Europa</i>—was truly a pleasure. I recommended <i>Kushiel's Dart</i> to fans of epic fantasy; now I'll go one step further and say that even straight up historical fiction fans can find enjoyment here. Carey's skill as a writer is something that transcends genre, and while <i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> is fantasy in name, it is fantastic by nature.<br /><br /><strong>My Reviews of Kushiel's Legacy:</strong><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40009839" rel="nofollow noopener">← <em>Kushiel's Dart</em></a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40009844" rel="nofollow noopener"><em>Kushiel's Avatar</em> →</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15200546598922442035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_150557441" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150557441" />
    <a title="Fey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2056399-fey"><img alt="Fey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333291219p2/2056399.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150557441?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fey" href="/user/show/2056399-fey">Fey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=bdsm">bdsm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2056399-fey?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150557441" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14598282159201087762">The second in the Kushiel's legacy series, continues on exactly where the first novel left off.<br/><br/>Phedre no Delaunay, now the comtesse de Montreve, comfortably living in her country home with Joscelin and her three chevaliers, and spending most of her time learning Habiru, in the hopes of discovering the key to freeing Hyacinth from the yeshuite curse. But then a parcel comes from Melisande Sharizhai - Phedre's sangoire cloak - and there is only one way to interpret it; Melisande's games of politic</span>
  <span id="freeText14598282159201087762" style="display:none">The second in the Kushiel's legacy series, continues on exactly where the first novel left off.<br /><br />Phedre no Delaunay, now the comtesse de Montreve, comfortably living in her country home with Joscelin and her three chevaliers, and spending most of her time learning Habiru, in the hopes of discovering the key to freeing Hyacinth from the yeshuite curse. But then a parcel comes from Melisande Sharizhai - Phedre's sangoire cloak - and there is only one way to interpret it; Melisande's games of politics and treachery and not yet finished, and she is inviting Phedre back into the game if she dares. And so Phedre goes back to the city, to take up service of Naamah again, to become again a courtesan and a spy. The first and greatest mystery being, who was it that aided Melisande's escape from Troyes le mont, and how far will Phedre need to go to find out.<br /><br />I have to say, I enjoyed this one just as much, if not more than Kushiel's Dart. Near the end of the previous I was almost lulled into thinking there would be no more adventure for Phedre, that she was settling down with Joscelin, and that would be it. But of course the adventure was far from over. And really what an amazing adventure this time.. So many new lands, cultures and people in this one. Which only makes me wonder how far she'd have to travel in the third book in order to beat it!<br /><br />As in the previous book there was no mercy for the heart, I believe Carey is one of those writers that will ruthlessly kill off beloved characters if it's important to the plot. She makes me cry so much, but I'm masochistic and I love a good cry, I can't help myself. Not telling who of course, you'll have to read it yourself and suffer the same as I did!<br /><br />Some of the aspects that interest me most about this series is the mythology and the magic. At times you could almost believe it's a fantasy world without magic, just myths and legends for them, and then - as with the master of the straits in the 1st book - something just jumps out at you to show you that magic can touch Phedre's world. And if magic can happen.. then are Phedre's visions of her deity Kushiel 'real'..? I am still hoping for this mythology to go further. I don't have as much interesting in the Yeshuite mythology, as so far it's a bit of a mimicry of Jewish/christian beliefs, and as just doesn't shine as much as the other more fantasy elements, but it still hasn't bothered me much, and it does create some interesting characters.<br /><br />If you were one of those, like I was, worried that the 2nd book would not live up to the 1st book.. just don't worry, keep reading, I promise it's great. And now I've proved to myself that it's just as good, (and I've got this review out of the way - my personal rule) I am now so so ready to jump into the 3rd book!!<br /><br /><br /><b>See my other reviews of <i>Kushiel's Legacy</i>:</b><br />← <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98663853" rel="nofollow noopener">#1 Kushiel's Dart</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150557579" rel="nofollow noopener">#3 Kushiel's Avatar</a> →<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14598282159201087762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98521888" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98521888" />
    <a title="Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/422087-bibliophile"><img alt="Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238517395p2/422087.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98521888?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibliophile" href="/user/show/422087-bibliophile">Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/422087-bibliophile?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/422087-bibliophile?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/422087-bibliophile?shelf=fantasy-and-scifi">fantasy-and-scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98521888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12674806467811354977"><i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> was my least favorite of Jacqueline Carey's trilogy featuring the <i>anguisette</i> Phedre no Delaunay. In this novel, the action shifts from Terre d'Ange to Carey's version of Venice (La Serenissima) so Phedre is free to display her snobbery and chauvinism to a grating degree (no one else is as beautiful as Angelines, no other place is as lovely, cultured, fashionable or interesting, no other language is as beautiful, yadda, yadda, yadda. By the time I'd read 700 pages of this, I want</span>
  <span id="freeText12674806467811354977" style="display:none"><i>Kushiel's Chosen</i> was my least favorite of Jacqueline Carey's trilogy featuring the <i>anguisette</i> Phedre no Delaunay. In this novel, the action shifts from Terre d'Ange to Carey's version of Venice (La Serenissima) so Phedre is free to display her snobbery and chauvinism to a grating degree (no one else is as beautiful as Angelines, no other place is as lovely, cultured, fashionable or interesting, no other language is as beautiful, yadda, yadda, yadda. By the time I'd read 700 pages of this, I wanted shut Phedre up in La Dolorosa myself just for being annoying!) And the "Mary Sue"ness of Phedre in this one is off the charts - EVERYONE falls in love with her (Illyrian pirates; Cretan princes, you name it!) <br /><br />Unfortunately, I think I like Melisande Shahrizai a lot more than I like Phedre or Phedre's boss Ysandre in this (and I think Melisande does have a point about how she'd make a fine queen!) Plus, there was not enough Joscelin in this for my tastes!<br /><br />I'm always a little weirded out in these books, by the way, by the co-existence of Bronze Age England with Renaissance (or even 18th century?) France and Italy and ancient Crete, as though none of the technological/religious developments in any country can migrate across their borders (yes, I get it that with the Master of the Straits, "England" stayed really isolated, but I don't understand how Crete is still basically Minoan Crete and yet it coexists with Dogal Venice. Really?)<br /><br />Lastly, Carey overuses certain words and phrases that drive me crazy: Examples: "well and so", "mayhap" and worst of all, "somewhat" when she means "something" which is "somewhat" that makes me have to mentally edit almost every sentence!<br /><br />And yet, go figure, I still thoroughly enjoyed this trilogy (and loved <i>Kushiel's Avatar</i>).</span>
  <a data-text-id="12674806467811354977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9971726027660823677">A solid 3.5 stars.<br/><br/>This is the 2nd book in the series and while good and true to the story line, it just seemed to drag on.<br/>It's a chunkster and I probably wasn't in the right head frame to be reading something that required me to remember a lot of names, places and previous story lines.<br/><br/>Jacqueline Carey is an excellent writer.   <span id="freeText9971726027660823677" style="display:none">A solid 3.5 stars.<br /><br />This is the 2nd book in the series and while good and true to the story line, it just seemed to drag on.<br />It's a chunkster and I probably wasn't in the right head frame to be reading something that required me to remember a lot of names, places and previous story lines.<br /><br />Jacqueline Carey is an excellent writer. <div id="review_3193074052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3193074052" />
    <a title="steph // bookplaits" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37929038-steph-bookplaits"><img alt="steph // bookplaits" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577746310p2/37929038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3193074052?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="steph // bookplaits" class="user" itemprop="url" name="steph // bookplaits" href="/user/show/37929038-steph-bookplaits">steph // bookplaits</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5382205-kushiel-s-chosen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37929038-steph-bookplaits?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37929038-steph-bookplaits?shelf=favourite-favourites">favourite-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3193074052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1771194764985172113">Although this isn’t a perfect book, it made me feel *so* deeply and think about the characters *so* much that I can’t rate it less than 5 stars!<br/><br/>I found Kushiel’s Chosen a lot easier to get into than the first book - because I knew the world and characters, it was easy to be swept away by the story immediately. Sure, the intricate politics still go over my head a bit, but I was captivated nonetheless!<br/><br/>Phèdre remains a compelling heroine and I still love her, despite her numerous flaws (e.g. how sh</span>
  <span id="freeText1771194764985172113" style="display:none">Although this isn’t a perfect book, it made me feel *so* deeply and think about the characters *so* much that I can’t rate it less than 5 stars!<br /><br />I found Kushiel’s Chosen a lot easier to get into than the first book - because I knew the world and characters, it was easy to be swept away by the story immediately. Sure, the intricate politics still go over my head a bit, but I was captivated nonetheless!<br /><br />Phèdre remains a compelling heroine and I still love her, despite her numerous flaws (e.g. how she treated a certain character in this story, and her views on non-D’Angelines). I also loved all the side characters, particularly Phèdre’s Boys – Fortun, Remy and Ti-Philippe ♥️ – and, of course, Joscelin. 😭♥️ Sometimes, when things got too much at various points, I’d pause to reread earlier scenes or even bits of Kushiel’s Dart. That’s a sure sign I’m invested in these characters!<br /><br />I won’t talk about the plot in case of spoilers, but overall I thought it was engaging; it was only around the middle of the story where I found it less interesting. But despite this, Carey has a way of writing such that I gasp and have to put my ereader/book down to compose myself when ~things~ are revealed or dramatic events occur. This is definitely helped by her use of short sentences, which give the book a snappy pace despite its length. When shocking things happened at the end of this chapter or that, you bet I had that ‘just one more chapter’ mindset each time!<br /><br />The villain in this story is so intriguing, and I really liked how Phèdre’s relationship with her was explored! The line between love/desire and hate can be a fine one indeed.<br /><br />I’m waiting for the next book to become available at the library because I’ve seen that these books are being rereleased later this year, so I’ll purchase them for my collection then!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1771194764985172113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1906969060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1906969060" />
    <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos"><img alt="Sotiris Karaiskos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407195235p2/18940246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1906969060?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sotiris Karaiskos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sotiris Karaiskos" href="/user/show/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos">Sotiris Karaiskos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781400109500" href="/book/show/7082268-kushiel-s-chosen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18940246-sotiris-karaiskos?shelf=historical-fantasy">historical-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1906969060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17486439268022756185">This second book of the series follows broadly the pattern of the first. We have a first part - almost one third of the book - especialy sexually charged where we are watching the political controversies and the various scheems that are knitting in Terre d'Ange, followed by a second where we go out on the road and wander around the world where the series takes place - who is essentially the world that we are living quite ... mixed - and we end up in the fight that resolve most things. In spite o</span>
  <span id="freeText17486439268022756185" style="display:none">This second book of the series follows broadly the pattern of the first. We have a first part - almost one third of the book - especialy sexually charged where we are watching the political controversies and the various scheems that are knitting in Terre d'Ange, followed by a second where we go out on the road and wander around the world where the series takes place - who is essentially the world that we are living quite ... mixed - and we end up in the fight that resolve most things. In spite of all these similarities, I believe that there will be several differences, and I dare to say that in this second book we are witnessing an upgrading as the writer becomes more daring - and I am not referring to the erotic scenes that are just a little more ... dangerous - in all areas, offering us something really epic.<br /><br />But this that fortunately for us not change at all is the amazing writing of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9237.Jacqueline_Carey" title="Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jacqueline Carey </a> that remains beautiful and touching. In this book, indeed, she is called to pass a test as the plot itself makes our dear Phedre wonder about many things as he goes through emotionally painful moments. This test, therefore, she passes it perfectly as she offers us with the description of very touching moments. That, you see, is also the main concern of this book: how emotional pain can one stand for something worthwhile, such as love. Difficult question, as you understand.<br /><br /> So the conclusion that comes out is that we again have an excellent result though I feel that this second part is slightly inferior to the former. Several times I felt that the writer repeats himself, recycling many of the ideas of the first book, while there are some excesses. Nevertheless for the second time <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9237.Jacqueline_Carey" title="Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jacqueline Carey </a> swept me away so much that I could not put anything less than five stars.<br /><br />Αυτό το δεύτερο βιβλίο της σειράς ακολουθεί σε γενικές γραμμές το μοτίβο του πρώτου. Έχουμε ένα πρώτο μέρος - σχεδόν το ένα τρίτο - ιδιαίτερα φορτισμένο σεξουαλικά όπου παρακολουθούμε τις πολιτικές διαμάχες και τα διάφορα σχέδια που πλέκονται στην Terre d'Ange, το οποίο ακολουθείται από ένα δεύτερο όπου βγαίνουμε στο δρόμο και περιφερόμαστε στον κόσμο που διαδραματίζεται η σειρά - ο οποίος ουσιαστικά είναι ο κόσμος που ζούμε αρκετά... ανακατεμένος - και καταλήγουμε στο μαχητικό ξεκαθάρισμα. Παρά όλες αυτές τις ομοιότητες πιστεύω ότι θα βρίσκονται και αρκετές διαφορές, τολμώ, μάλιστα, να πω ότι σε αυτό το δεύτερο βιβλίο γινόμαστε μάρτυρες μία μιας αναβάθμισης καθώς η συγγραφέας γίνεται πιο τολμηρή - και δεν αναφέρομαι στις ερωτικές σκηνές που γίνονται λίγο πιο... επικίνδυνες - σε όλους τους τομείς προσφέροντας μας κάτι πραγματικά επικό.<br /><br />Αυτό, όμως, ευτυχώς για εμάς δεν αλλάζει καθόλου είναι η καταπληκτική γραφή της <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9237.Jacqueline_Carey" title="Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacqueline Carey</a> που παραμένει όμορφη και συγκινητική. Σε αυτό το βιβλίο, μάλιστα, καλείται να περάσει μία δοκιμασία καθώς η ίδια η πλοκή κάνει την αγαπητή μας Φαίδρα να αναρωτιέται για πολλά πράγματα καθώς περνάει συναισθηματικά επώδυνες στιγμές. Αυτήν τη δοκιμασία, λοιπόν, την περνάει με άριστα καθώς μας προσφέρει την περιγραφή πολύ συγκινητικών στιγμών. Αυτός, βλέπετε, είναι και ο βασικός προβληματισμός αυτού του βιβλίου: πόσο συναισθηματικό πόνο μπορεί να αντέξει κάποιος μπροστά σε κάτι που αξίζει τον κόπο, όπως για παράδειγμα τον έρωτα. Δύσκολα πράγματα όπως καταλαβαίνετε.<br /><br /> Οπότε το συμπέρασμα που βγαίνει είναι ότι έχουμε πάλι ένα άριστο αποτέλεσμα αν και νιώθω ότι αυτό το δεύτερο μέρος είναι ελαφρώς υποδεέστερο του πρώτου. Αρκετές φορές ένιωσα ότι η συγγραφέας επαναλαμβάνεται, ανακυκλώνοντας πολλές από τις ιδέες του πρώτου βιβλίου, ενώ δε λείπουν και κάποιες υπερβολές. Παρ' όλα αυτά για δεύτερη φορά η <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9237.Jacqueline_Carey" title="Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacqueline Carey</a> με παρέσυρε τόσο που μου είναι αδύνατο να βάλω κάτι λιγότερο από 5 αστέρια.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17486439268022756185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1156884213" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1156884213" />
    <a title="gio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23204207-gio"><img alt="gio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597613414p2/23204207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1156884213?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gio" href="/user/show/23204207-gio">gio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22317536-kushiel-s-chosen">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1156884213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15965443518196049923"><br/>-Phèdre's pms was terrible<br/>- Joscelin is still a cutie patootie<br/>- Melisande is the best villain ever<br/><br/>I liked it less than Kushiel's Dart. That's the only certain thing I can tell you to be honest. <br/><br/>The problem for me was Phèdre. Even in the first book I had liked her less than the so-called secondary characters and she certainly didn't do anything to "redeem" herself in my eyes this time around. It's not a matter of her beliefs or her personality, but simply of taste: I do not feel like I can care f</span>
  <span id="freeText15965443518196049923" style="display:none"><br>-Phèdre's pms was terrible<br>- Joscelin is still a cutie patootie<br>- Melisande is the best villain ever<br><br>I liked it less than Kushiel's Dart. That's the only certain thing I can tell you to be honest. <br><br>The problem for me was Phèdre. Even in the first book I had liked her less than the so-called secondary characters and she certainly didn't do anything to "redeem" herself in my eyes this time around. It's not a matter of her beliefs or her personality, but simply of taste: I do not feel like I can care for her nor she makes me want to. <br><br>This brings me to an interesting (at least for me lol) point. Carey's prose makes me think of Rothfuss'. The stories couldn't be more different (even though I think Kvothe would take an interest in Phèdre :P) but they do have in common a beautiful prose and a first person point of view, since it's the main character that tells their own story. (Not to mention how vain they both are). In both cases I felt like the main characters kept pointing out their abilities way too much for me to actually like them. Does this make sense?<br><br>In fact, to be honest, I liked Melisande way more than Phèdre. And while I like that the author choose two strong female characters to lead this game, I did not like how Phèdre threated other people, especially Joscelin. I liked that the author choose to address this problem, because it was quite clear that Joscelin and Phèdre's relationship was bound to be troubled, at least because of their "calling", but I liked Joscelin's choices far more than Phèdre's. She knew that Joscelin's would not understand her choices and while I liked that she got that, I did not like all those talks about "the pains of the soul" that brought her pleasure. I do not care you're Kushiel's Dart, you do not hurt my puppy and be happy because you're hurting him and yourself in the process. <br><br>Joscelin is precious, you little bastard.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455904093ra/18167309.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, if I hear the sentence "the training of the Night Court is so blah blah" another time I'll kill someone.<br><br>I liked the plot. I think it was more predictable this time around, because in Kushiel's Dart I was surprised by pretty much everything, while this time I could tell what Melisande was plotting, but I think it was a bit more...polished in some parts. If I had some problems with the pace of book 1 I found book 2 much more refined and with more balance to its different parts at least. <br><br>I missed some characters. I felt like I got to see more of Phèdre and Joscelin's character development, but at the same time I missed Hyacinthe's humour and the comical relief he brought. <br><br><i>"Go and tell everybody how you hartred towards Melisande was misplaced in book 1."</i>: actually I kind of like hating her. Does that make sense? I liked her in this installment and I liked her clever games. I do not think there are many villains I loathe and love as much as I do when it comes to Melisande. I guess it's partly due to how well developed her character is and also to how much she outshined the main character in this case. That <i>"Hello, Phèdre."</i> is probably the best line in the whole book. <br><br>Overall I liked Kushiel's Dart more, especially when it comes to the characters and the intrigue, but I did find Chosen to be better written and more polished. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15965443518196049923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=other-adult-fantasy">other-adult-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=own-it">own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1637878-allison-the-allure-of-books?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66322428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5664057283481003711">I was almost scared to read this, because I was just sure it wouldn't be able to measure up to Kushiel's Dart. If I'd known how wrong I was, I wouldn't have waited two months to pick it up! I probably won't be able to wait even a week to start the third one.<br/><br/>So often, books in a series have different vibes, and the feelings you get while reading them are so varied that its hard to consider them connected. Not so with these, Kushiel's Chosen was very much a continuation of the first, and I can't r</span>
  <span id="freeText5664057283481003711" style="display:none">I was almost scared to read this, because I was just sure it wouldn't be able to measure up to Kushiel's Dart. If I'd known how wrong I was, I wouldn't have waited two months to pick it up! I probably won't be able to wait even a week to start the third one.<br /><br />So often, books in a series have different vibes, and the feelings you get while reading them are so varied that its hard to consider them connected. Not so with these, Kushiel's Chosen was very much a continuation of the first, and I can't really give it any higher praise. I picked up where I left off, feeling the exact same way about all the characters and immediately picked up my deep emotional connections to most of them.<br /><br />Carey has such an awesome way of writing things. You spend the first 300 pages (give or take) knowing something awful is coming, and to some degree I'm sure everyone tries to figure out what that might be...but then all of a sudden it hits out of nowhere and spins the story out of control straight to the end. It is CRAZY. I loved that about Dart, and loved it in this one also.<br /><br />Its also a great mark of her writing abilities that she can display such a wide emotional range in these characters. Seduction and sex are these peoples' occupations as homage to their gods, and as such the acts are displayed as duty, not pleasure. But, when the emotions are real, such beauty and love shine through.<br /><br />I can't recommend this series enough to the people willing to take a risk on such an original and fascinating storyline.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5664057283481003711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4062226-jeannette?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
